Jamison Brereton

3 (194)
A╠Дpr─▒╠Д
Gr╠еtsamada
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except jagat─л 7
This is one of the ten so-called ─Аpr─л hymns in the R╠еgveda, a litany recited at the animal sacrifice: the subjects of the verses appear in a fixed order, each signaled by a key word (italicized in the following translation), though the exact wording of each differs from hymn to hymn. This type of flexible composition around a set of fixed themes and terms in a fixed order may give us some insight into R╠еgvedic compo
sitional techniques. This version is somewhat fuller and verbally richer than most, encouraged by the relatively capacious measures of triс╣гс╣нubh meter. For a minimalist version, see I.13.

Jamison Brereton Notes

─Аpr─л

рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдВрд╡реЗрджрд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдпрд╛рдВрд╕рдорд┐рджреНрдзрдГ рд╕рдореНрдпрдХреН рджреАрдкреНрддрдГ рдПрддрдиреНрдирд╛рдордХреЛрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рдирд┐рд╣рд┐рддрдГ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрд┐рддрдГ рд╕рдиреН рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд┐рд╕- рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгрд┐ рднреБрд╡рдирд╛рдирд┐рднреВрддрдЬрд╛рддрд╛рдирд┐рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдЩреН рдЕрднрд┐рдореБрдЦрдГрд╕рдиреН рдЕрд╕реНрдерд╛рддреН рддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддрд┐ рдпрдерд╛рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрдЬрдирд╛рдГ рдкрд╢реНрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╡реГ- рджреНрдзреЛрднрд╡реНрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪ рд╕реЛрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрд╣реЛрддрд╛рд╣реЛрдордирд┐рд╖реНрдкрд╛рджрдХреЛрджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдорд╛рд╣реНрд╡рд╛рддрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкрд╛рд╡рдХрдГ рд╢реЛрдзрдХрдГ рдкреНрд░рджрд┐рд╡рдГ рдкреБрд░рд╛рдгрдГ рд╕реБрдореЗрдзрд╛рдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮреЛрджреЗрд╡реЛрджреНрдпреЛрддрдорд╛рдирдГ рдПрд╡рдореНрдорд╣рд╛рдиреБрднрд╛рд╡реЛрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рдЕрд░реНрд╣рдиреН рдпрд╛рдЧрдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрдГ рд╕рдиреН рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдпрдЬрддреБ рдЕрддреНрд░рдп- рд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рджреАрдиреНрдкреВрдЬрдпрддреБ рее рез рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni, the well-kindled, plural ced upon (the altar of) the earth, stands in the presence of all beings; the invoker (of the gods), the purifier, the ancient, the intelligent, the divine; let the venerable Agni minister to the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

─Аpris: cf. 1.142; 1.188

Jamison Brereton

Agni, kindled, deposited on the earth, has stood up facing all beings. The pure, very wise Hotar from olden daysтАФlet Agni the god sacrifice to the gods, (himself) deserving (it).

Griffith

AGNI is set upon the earth well kindled; he standeth in the presence of all beings.
Wise, ancient, God, the Priest and Purifier, let Agni serve the Gods for he is worthy.

Oldenberg

Agni being kindled, set down on the earth, has stood up with his face towards all worlds. May the Hotri, the purifier, the ancient, wise one, may god Agni sacrifice to the gods, he who is worthy (of being the sacrificer).

Geldner

Entflammt, auf die Erde niedergesetzt steht Agni da allen Wesen zugewandt. Seit alter Zeit der lautere, hochweise Hotri soll Agni, der Gott, die G├╢tter als W├╝rdige verehren.

Grassmann

Entz├╝ndet Agni, eingesetzt auf Erden, zu allen Wesen hingewandt, erhob sich, Der weise Priester flammend wie vor Alters; es ehre Agni, er der Gott, die G├╢tter.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the bright Nar─Б┼Ыaс╣Гsa, illuminating the receptacles (of the offering) making manifest by his greatness the three radiant (regions) and diffusing the oblation at the season of sacrifice with butter-dispensing purpose, satisfy the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Nar─Б┼Ыaс╣Гsa: in the preceding s┼лktas, tan┼лnap─Бt is the second person nification of Agni addressed; in this s┼лkta, he is omitted

Jamison Brereton

Nar─Б┼Ыaс╣Гsa, who anoints, counter(part) to the foundations (of the earth) and to the three heavens with his greatness, he of lovely
flames,
with his ghee-sprinkling mind wetting the oblationтАФat the head of the sacrifice let him anoint the gods altogether.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda a is supposed to contain a lexeme pr├бti тИЪa├▒j governing dh─Б╠Бm─Бni, but this would be the only ex. of the verbal idiom in the RV. I therefore take pr├бti as governing dh─Б╠Бm─Бni тАШfoundationsтАЩ, in a parallel expression to tisr├│ d├нvaс╕е pr├бti in b. I supply тАЬof the earthтАЭ with dh─Б╠Бm─Бni on the basis of I.22.16 dh─Б╠Бmabhiс╕е pr╠еthivy─Б╠Бс╕е. The participle a├▒j├бn would be used absolutely and anticipate s├бm anaktu in d. The early part of the hymn has a tendency to station present participles at p─Бda ends, and not always with obj. (1d ├бrhan, our 2a, 2c und├бn, 3a ├бrhan).

Griffith

May Narasamsa lighting up the chambers, bright in his majesty through threefold heaven,
Steeping the gift with oil diffusing purpose, bedew the Gods at chiefest time of worship.

Oldenberg

Nar├вsamsa, anointing the abodes (of the sacrifice), equal by his greatness to the three heavens, endowed with beautiful light, moistening the offering, his mind being intent on scattering ghritaтАФmay he anoint the gods on the summit of sacrifice.

Geldner

Narasamsa, der die Formen des Opfers einweiht, der an Gr├╢├Яe die drei Himmel aufwiegt, der sch├╢nstrahlende, der mit schmalztriefenden Gedanken die Opferspende netzt, er soll an der Spitze des Opfers die G├╢tter vereinen.

Der M├дnnerpreis, der alle St├дtten ausschm├╝ckt, mit seinem Glanz bestrahlend die drei Himmel, In spr├╝hnder Lust mit Fett das Opfer netzend, im Opferanbruch salbe er die G├╢tter.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni, who are the venerable ─лс╕╖ita, do you, with mind favourably disposed towards us, offer today sacrifice to the gods, before the human (ministrant priest) as such, bring hither the company of the Maruts, the undecaying Indra, to whom, seated on the sacred grass, do you priests offer worship.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Solemnly invoked by (our) mind, o Agni, deserving (it), sacrifice today to the gods for us in front of the descendant of Manu.
Convey here the unstirrable troop of the Maruts. You men, sacrifice to Indra who sits on the ritual grass.

Griffith

Adored in heart, as is thy right, O Agni, serve the Gods first to-day before the mortal.
Bring thou the Marut host. Ye men do worship to Indra seated on the grass, eternal.

Oldenberg

Being magnified 1 in our mind, Agni, sacrifice for us to-day to the gods before the human (sacrificer) 2, thou who art worthy (of being the sacrificer). Conduct hither the unshakable host of the Maruts. Sacrifice, O men, to Indra who sits on the Barhis.

Geldner

Von uns im Geiste als der W├╝rdige berufen, sollst du, Agni, heute die G├╢tter noch vor dem menschlichen Hotri verehren. Fahr du die unentwegte Schar der Marut her! Verehret, ihr M├дnner, den Indra, wenn er auf dem Barhis sitzt!

Grassmann

Erfleht von uns mit Inbrunst, kund’ger Agni, verehre heut die G├╢tter vor dem Menschen, So fahre her die Marutschar, die feste; den Indra, ehrt, o M├дnner, der die Streu liebt.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDivine grass, let the Vasus, the VI┼Ыvedevas, the adorable ─Аditya, sit upon this flourishing, invigrating, well-grown, sacred grass, strewn for the sakeof wealth upon this altar, and sprinkled with butter.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Divine grass: the barhis, or a person nification of Agni

Jamison Brereton

O divine Ritual GrassтАФgrowing strong, affording good heroes, having a lovely burden [=the gods], strewn on this altar here for wealth.
Good ones, sit here on it, which is anointed with gheeтАФall you gods, ─Аdityas, worthy of the sacrifice.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The apparent loc. v├йd─л (so Pp.) should probably be read v├йdi for metrical reasons (see Oldenberg: тАЬnur angeblich Pragс╣ЫhyaтАЭ [Noten]; Proleg. 456). AiG III.154-55 is skeptical about a loc. -─л to -i-stems and suggests that this, the clearest example, is actually to be explained by haplology from *v├йdy[─Бm] asy─Б╠Бm, which seems highly unlikely, esp. since it would make the cadence metrically irreparable. I think we have to take this form as given and as a locative (not instr.), with a metrically short final vowel, which may result from shortening in hiatus. For a similar ex. see bh┼л╠Бm─л (/ -i) in IX.61.10 and comm. thereon.

The last p─Бda contains a mixture of voc. (dev─Б ─Бdity─Бс╕е) and nom. (yaj├▒├нy─Бsaс╕е), with p─Бda-initial v├н┼Ыve ambiguous, since the accent may derive from its position. The tr. does not reflect this case mixture, since a meticulous separation would be fussy and serve no purpose.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet the divine doors, spacious and easily accessible, and to be saluted with prostrations, be set open; let them be celebrated as expansive, uninjurable, and conferring sanctity upon the illustrious class (of worshippers), possessed of virtuous progeny.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let them gape open widelyтАФthe Divine Doors, easy to approachтАФwhen invoked with reverences.
Expansive, let the unaging ones spread forth, purifying their own тАЬcolorтАЭ [=people] (so that it is) glorious, rich in heroes.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Oldenberg points out, supr─Бyaс╣З├б- is metrically bad here and worse in several other occurrences; it should be read *supray─Бс╣З├б-, which presumably belongs to тИЪy─Б, not тИЪi.

I take the adjectives in d (ya┼Ы├бsaс╣Г suv─л╠Бram) as proleptic, the result of the purification, though this interpr. isnтАЩt strictly necessary.

Griffith

Wide be the Doors, the Goddesses, thrown open, easy to pass, invoked, through adorations,
Let them unfold, expansive, everlasting, that sanctify the class famed, rich in heroes.

Oldenberg

May the divine doors which are easily passable, open themselves wide when invoked with adoration. May they, the far-embracing, undecaying ones, open wide, purifying our glorious race 1 which is rich in valiant men.

Geldner

Es sollen sich die g├╢ttlichen, gern betretenen Tore weit auftun, unter Verneigung angerufen. Die vielfassenden, alterlosen sollen sich breit machen, die angesehene, aus Meistern bestehende Kaste heiligend.

Grassmann

Die G├╢tterthore m├╢gen weit sich aufthun, die angerufnen, sch├╢n bewegt durch Andacht, Die grossen ew’gen m├╢gen weit sich ├╢ffnen, erregend sch├╢nes, m├дnnerreiches Gl├дnzen.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬIn regard of our good deeds, Day and Night, perpetually reverenced, are interweaving in concert, like two famous feminine le weavers, the extended thread, (to complete) the web of the sacrifice, liberal yielders (of rewards), containers of water.тАЭ

Like two famous feminine le weavers: vayyeva raс╣Зvite = vayya iva v─Бnaku┼Ыale iva ┼Ыabdite, stute

Jamison Brereton

Strengthened of old for us, Dawn and Night, like happy weavers on target at their labors,
jointly interweaving the stretched thread, the ornament of the sacrificeтАФ the good milk-cows rich in milk.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In b vayy├иva belongs to a vс╣Ыk─л╠Б-type stem vay─л╠Б- тАШweaverтАЩ, here in the dual. Oldenberg suggests that it doesnтАЩt really matter if we analyze it as vay├н y─Б iva, with masc. du., or vay├н ye (i)va with fem. du., but given that the other adjectives in the hemistich, ukс╣гit├й тАж raс╣Зvit├й, are feminine in form and that uс╣г─Б╠Бsan├бkt─Б is regularly fem., the latter seems more likely.

The vs. lacks a finite verb and there is no verbal form, finite or participial, to govern ├бp─Бс╣Гsi тАШlaborsтАЩ in a. Most tr. supply тАШworkтАЩ vel sim., but I think itтАЩs possible that s─Бdh├║ is an adverbial predicate, тАЬon targetтАЭ in the published translation, and that it loosely governs ├бp─Бс╣Гsi.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рджреИрд╡реНрдпрд╛ рджрд┐рд╡рд┐рднрд╡реЛрджрд┐рд╡реНрдпреЛрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреНрджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рджрдЧреНрдиреЗрд░реНрдЬрд╛рддреМ рд╣реЛрддрд╛рд░рд╛рдЖрд╣реНрд╡рд╛рддрд╛рд░реМ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВрд╣реЛрдордирд┐рд╖реНрдкрд╛рджрдХреМрд╡рд╛- рдЧреНрдиреА рдкрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рд╡рд╛рдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реНрдпреМ рдкреНрд░рдердорд╛рдкреНрд░рдердордВрдпрд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпреМ рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрд░рд╛рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрддрдореМ рд╡рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд░рд╛рдкреНрд░рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╡рдкреБрд╖реМрджреЗрд╡рд╛рд╡реГрдЪрд╛ рдордиреНрддреНрд░реЗрдг рдЛ- рдЬреБрдЕрд╡рд┐рдХрд▓рдВ рдпрдерд╛рддрдерд╛рд╕рдореНрдпрдХреН рдпрдХреНрд╖рддрдГ рдкреВрдЬрдпрддрдГ рдЛрддреБрдерд╛рддрддреНрддрджреГрддреМ рддрддреНрд░рддрддреНрд░рдХрд╛рд▓реЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдпрд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдиреН рдпрдЬрдиреНрддреМ рджреЗрд╡реМ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдирд╛рднрд╛рдирд╛рднреМ рдЙрддреНрддрд░рд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдЕрдзрд┐рдЙрдкрд░рд┐ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реБрд╕рд╛рдиреБрд╖реБрд╕рдореБрдЪреНрдЫреНрд░рд┐рддреЗрд╖реБ рдкреНрд░рджреЗрд╢реЗрд╖реБрдЧрд╛рд░реНрд╣рдкрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ рд╕рдо- рдЮреНрдЪрддрдГ рд╕рдорд╛рдЩреНрдХреНрддрд╛рдВ рдЕрдЮреНрдЪрддреЗрд░реНрд▓реЗрдЯреНрдпрдбрд╛рдЧрдордГ рее рен рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet the two divine invokers of the gods, the first (to be reverenced), most wise, sincerely worshipping with sacred texts, most excellent in form, offering homage to the gods in due season, present oblations in the three high plural ces upon the navel of the earth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Two divine invokers of the gods: the person nified fires of earth and the firmament, under the character of, two ministeringpriests; the navel of the earth: this is the usual altar; the three high plural ces: s─Бnuс╣гu triс╣гu, are the three sacred fires: g─Бrhapatya, ─Бhavan─лya and dakс╣гiс╣З─Б

Jamison Brereton

The first two Divine Hotars, more knowing, more wondrous, together will sacrifice rightly with their chant.
Sacrificing to the gods according to the proper season, they jointly
anoint them on the navel of the earth, on the three backs (of the fires).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Renou and Witzel Got┼Н supply тАШsacrificeтАЩ as the obj. of s├бm a├▒jataс╕е, but since acc. dev─Б╠Бn is already available and was the obj. of exactly the same verb in 2d (s├бm anaktu dev─Б╠Бn), this is unnecessary.

Griffith

Let the two heavenly Heralds, first, most wise, most fair, present oblation duly with the sacred verse,
Worshipping God at ordered seasons decking them at three high places at the centre of the earth.

Oldenberg

May the two divine Hotris, the first ones, very knowing, very marvellous, perform the sacrifice rightly with their (sacrificial) verse. Sacrificing to the gods they anoint (them) 1, observing the right time, on the navel of the Earth, over the three ridges (of the three worlds).

Geldner

Die beiden ersten g├╢ttlichen Hotri, die kundigeren, m├╢gen in Versen richtig zusammen opfern in sch├╢nerer Gestalt. Indem sie zur rechten Zeit zusammen opfern, m├╢gen sie die G├╢tter vereinen im Nabel der Welt an den drei Feuererh├╢hungen.

Grassmann

Die G├╢tterpriester, weisheitsvoll die pr├дchtigen, sie beid’ als erste eilen vorw├дrts mit Gesang, Sie tr├дnken opfernd rechter Art die G├╢tterschar, auf drei Alt├дren in der Erde Heiligthum.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬMay the three goddesses, Sarasvat─л, perfecting our understanding, the divine iс╕╖─Б, and all-impressive Bh─Бrat─л, having come to our dwelling, protect this faultless rite, (offered) for our welfare.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Sarasvat─л, who sends our poetic thought to its target, divine Iс╕Н─Б, Bh─Бrat─л outstripping allтАФ

let the three goddesses, having sat down on this ritual grass here, with their own power protect (its?) unbroken shelter.

Jamison Brereton Notes

s─Бdh├бya(nti) in p─Бda a and svadh├бy─Б in c occupy the same metrical position and echo each other.

Griffith

Sarasvati who perfects our devotion, Ila divine, Bharati all surpassing,-
Three Goddesses, with power inherent, seated, protect this holy Grass, our flawless refuge!

рдкрд┐рд╢рдЩреНрдЧрд░реВрдкрдГ рд╕реБрд╡рд░реНрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдГ рдирд╛рдирд╛рд░реВрдкреЛрд╡рд╛рд╕реБрднрд░рдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирдпрдЬреНрдЮрдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирднрд░рдгреЛрд╡рд╛ рд╡рдпреЛрдзрд╛рд╡рдпрд╕реЛрдиреНрдирд╕реНрдп рдзрд╛рд░рдпрд┐рддрд╛рджрд╛рддрд╛рд╡рд╛ рд╢реНрд░реБрд╖реНрдЯреАрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдЧреБрдгрдГ рд╡реАрд░реЛрд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдзрдореАрд░рдпрд┐рддрд╛ рджреЗрд╡рдХрд╛рдордГ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рдХрд╛рдореНрдпрдиреНрддреЗрдпреЗрдирддрд╛рджреГрд╢рдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░реЛ- рдЬрд╛рдпрддреЗ рдЬрдпрддрд╛рдореБрддреНрдкрд╛рджреНрдпрддрд╛рдиреНрддреНрд╡рд╖реНрдЯреБрд░рдиреБрдЧреНрд░рд╣рд╛рддреН рд╕рдЪрддреНрд╡рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдПрддрдиреНрдирд╛рдордХреЛрджреЗрд╡реЛрд╕реНрдореЗрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдиреНрдирд╛рднрд┐рдЩреНрдХреБрд▓рд╕реНрдпрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдХрд╛рдореНрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдВ рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛рджрд┐рд░реВрдкрд╛рдВрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдпрддреБ рд╡рд┐рдореБрдЮреНрдЪрддреБ рд╡рд┐рддрд░рддреНрд╡рд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рдЕрдердЕрдкрд┐рдЪрджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВрд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдкрд╛рдереЛрдиреНрдирдордкреНрдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреЗрддреБ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреБ рдЕрдкрд┐рдГрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рд╕рдореНрдмрдзреНрдпрддреЗ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреНрд╡рд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее реп рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay a tawny-hued, well-grown (son), the bestower of food, active, manly, a worshipper of the gods, be born; may Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б prolong for us a continuous (line of) progeny, and may the food of the gods come also to us.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Of tawny form, of good support [/easy to bear], conferring vigor, a hero desirous of the gods is born because of (TvastarтАЩs?/the godsтАЩ?)
attentive listeningтАФ
let Tvaс╣гс╣нar unbind (our) navel and release the offspring to us. Then let (the sacrificial victim) go into the pen of the gods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

subh├бra- here is used in a different sense (or senses) from the same word in 4b, where it referred to the good burden, that is, the seated gods, that the barhis was bearing. Here I think there is a pun: the hero is тАШeasy to bearтАЩ, that is, his birth, depicted in p─Бda b, was easy. But the hero so born provides good support to those who depend on him.

With Renou, I tr. v├н с╣гyatu in two slightly different senses with two different objects: тАШunbindтАЩ with тАШnavelтАЩ (n─Б╠Бbhim), referring to the technicalities of the birth process, and тАШreleaseтАЩ with тАШoffspringтАЩ (praj─Б╠Бm), referring to the results of birth.

The Tvaс╣гс╣нar verse in ─Аpr─л hymns generally directly concerns only his participation in the birth process (see I.142.10, III.4.9=VII.2.9, X.110.9, X.142.10; our p─Бdas abc). Releasing the sacrificial animal and escorting it to (the fold/pen of) the gods is properly the province of the post (тАЬLord of the Forest,тАЭ v├бnasp├бtiс╕е, 10a), and that expression (тАЬgo to [the fold of] the godsтАЭ) is a euphemism for the animalтАЩs death. However, note X.70.9-10, where both Tvaс╣гс╣нar and the Lord of the Forest convey the animal to the fold of the gods (dev─Б╠Бn─Бm p─Б╠Бthaс╕е). Like X.70.9 our p─Бda d implies that the journey of the sacrifical animal (that is, its death) occurs under the auspices of Tvaс╣гс╣нar, and in fact, given the apparent temporal/logical connector ├бth─Б beginning p─Бda d, the implication is that the offspring born in abc is to undertake this journey. This seems rather muddled: our new (human) offspring is not the sacrificial animal. I think the roles of Tvaс╣гс╣нar and the Lord of the Forest were quite distinct, but conflations like this could occur because the Tvaс╣гс╣нar and Vanaspati vss. are always adjacent in ─Аpr─л hymns and because the vocabulary is similar: Tvaс╣гс╣нarтАЩs v├н тИЪs─Б тАШunbind/releaseтАЩ and VanaspatiтАЩs ├бva тИЪsс╣Ыj тАШrelease/dischargeтАЩ. The fact that the victim is usually not overly expressed (presumably a euphemistic avoidance) makes confusion all the more likely.

Griffith

Born is the pious hero swift of hearing, like gold in hue, well formed, and full of vigour.
May Tvastar lengthen our line and kindred, and may they reach the place which Gods inhabit.

Oldenberg

Through (the god’s) hearing (our prayer) a manly son is born (to us), tawny-coloured, rich in gain, bringing vigour, loving the gods. May Tvashtri deliver for us a son, the navel (i. e. the tie that binds generations together), and may he then go to the abode of the gods.

Geldner

Ein br├дunlicher Sohn, der nicht zur Last f├дllt, ein St├дrkebringer, wird p├╝nktlich geboren, ein g├╢tterliebender. Tvastri soll uns den Nabel von Nachkommenschaft entbinden. Nunmehr soll es in die Obhut der G├╢tter ├╝bergehen!

Grassmann

Von Farbe braun, gedrungen, Leben spendend ersteht sogleich der Held die G├╢tter liebend, Tvaschtar begl├╝ck’ uns Kinder und Verwandtschaft, und dann gelang’ er zu der G├╢tter Wohnsitz.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay Agni, who is Vanaspati, approving (of our rite), approach; and by his especial acts fully dress the victim; may the divine immolator convey the burnt-offering to the gods, knowing it to have been thrice consecrated.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

By his especial acts: agnir-haviс╕е s┼лday─Бti pra dh─лbhiс╕е =Agni, who is the supporter, or the instrumental ument of cooking or maturing fitly, cooks the oblation of the nature of the victim with various acts, which are the means of cooking; he dresses the oblation, not under-dressing nor over-dressing it: agniс╕е p─Бkadharo haviс╕е pa┼Ыur┼лpam karmaviс╣гe┼Ыaiс╕е p─Бkas─Бdhanaiс╕е prakarс╣гeс╣Зa s┼лday─Бti kс╣г─Бrayati ap─Бk─Бdhikap─Бdir─Бhityena haviс╕е pacati; the divine immolator: daivyaс╕е ┼Ыamit─Б: ┼Ыamit─Б = the person n who kills the victim; Agni is the immolator of the gods: dev─Бn─Бm ┼Ыamit─Б; thice consecrated: tridh─Б samaktam = thrice anointed or sprinkled; the three rites or ceremonies are termed: upastaraс╣Зa, avad─Бna, abhigh─Бraс╣Зa

Jamison Brereton

The Lord of the Forest [=sacrificial post] stands by on releasing (the victim). Agni will sweeten the oblation with his poetic thoughts.
Let him who knows (the way) lead the thrice-anointed oneтАФ(let) the divine Butcher (lead) the oblation up to the gods.

Griffith

Vanaspati shall stand anear and start us, and Agni with his arts prepare oblation.
Let the skilled heavenly Immolator forward unto the Gods the offering thrice anointed.

Oldenberg

1 May the tree (i. e. the sacrificial post) stand by, letting loose (the offering which goes to the gods). May Agni make the offering ready in consequence of our prayers. May the prescient divine butcher carry the thrice-anointed offering to the gods.

Geldner

Der Baum soll dabei stehen, der das Tier freigibt. Agni m├╢ge mit Verst├дndnis die Opfergabe gar machen. Der g├╢ttliche Zurichter soll des Weges kundig die dreifach besalbte Opfergabe den G├╢ttern zuf├╝hren.

Grassmann

Der Pfosten stehe, Opfertrank ergiessend, den Guss versch├╢ne Agni durch Gebete; Dreimal gesalbtes Opfer f├╝hre kundig den G├╢ttern zu der g├╢ttliche Besorger.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI sprinkle the butter, for butter is his birth-plural ce; he is nourished by butter; butter is his radiance; Agni, showerer (of benefits), bring the gods to the offered oblation; exhilarate them; convey to them the offering that has been reverently sanctified.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Cf. Yajurveda 17.88; dh─Бma - dwelling, or radiance; alternative reading: Adhvaryu, or priest, bring hither Agni to the oblation; exhilarate him; (and say to him). Showerer (of blessings), convey the consecrated oblation (to the gods).

Jamison Brereton

Ghee is attached (to him); ghee is his womb. He is propped in ghee, and ghee is his foundation.
In accord with your own power convey (the gods) hither; invigorate
yourself. O bull, you will convey the oblation, prepared with the
sv─Бh─Б-call.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The -si form vakс╣гi would be better tr. as an impv. тАЬconvey,тАЭ rather than a subj. тАЬyou will conveyтАЭ as in the published translation

Griffith

Oil has been mixt: oil is his habitation. In oil he rests: oil is his proper province.
Come as thy wont is: O thou Steer, rejoice thee; bear off the oblation duly consecrated.

Oldenberg

He 1 is joined with ghrita 2. His womb (on the altar) is ghrita. He rests on ghrita. His abode is ghrita. Carry hither (the gods) according to thy wont! Rejoice 3! Carry, O bull, the offering, over which the Sv├вh├в has been spoken, (to the gods).

Geldner

Das Schmalz geh├╢rt zu ihm, Schmalz ist sein Mutterscho├Я, in Schmalz steckt er sich, Schmalz ist sein Element. Aus eigener Vollmacht fahre die G├╢tter her, erg├╢tze dich, bef├╢rdere unter Svaharuf die Opferspende, du Bulle!

Grassmann

Es str├╢mt die Butter, Butter ist sein Ruhsitz, in Butter weilt er, Butter ist sein Wohnhaus; Auf eignen Antrieb fahre her, erfreu dich, und fahr, o Stier, den Trank geweiht durch Heilruf.

Elizarenkova

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдЬреЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдпрдЬреНрдЮ рдореЗрдВ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рдЙрдкрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдкрд░реЛрдкрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд╛ рдЖрд╢реНрд░рдп рдХрд┐рдпреЗ рд╣реБрдП рдФрд░реЛрдВ рдХреЛ рд╕реБрдЦреА рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рдЖрдк рднреА рдЙрдирд╕реЗ рдЙрдкрдХрд╛рд░ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдФрд░ рдЖрдирдиреНрджрд┐рдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ реерезрезрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдФрд░ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЖрдЪрд░рдг рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдкрд┐рдЫрд▓реЗ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рд╣реИ, рдпрд╣ рдЬрд╛рдирдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рджреВрд╕рд░реЗ рдордгреНрдбрд▓ рдореЗрдВ рддреАрд╕рд░рд╛ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рддреЗрдИрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╡реГрд╖рдн рдпрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд╣рд╛рдХреГрддрдВ рд╣рд╡реНрдпрдВ рд╡рдХреНрд╖рд┐ рд╕ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдордиреБрд╖реНрд╡рдзрдорд╛ рд╡рд╣ред рдпрдерд╛рд╜рд╣рдВ рдШреГрддрдВ рдорд┐рдорд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ рддрдерд╛ рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕реЗрдХреНрддреБрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫ рдпрдерд╛рд╜рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрд░реНрдШреГрддрдВ рдШреГрддрдореБ рдпреЛрдирд┐рд░реНрдШреГрддреЗ рд╢реНрд░рд┐рддреЛ рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдзрд╛рдорд╛рд╜рд╕реНрддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рддреЗрди рддреНрд╡рдВ рдорд╛рджрдпрд╕реНрд╡ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдШреГрддрдореН) рдЖрдЬреНрдпрдореН (рдорд┐рдорд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ) рдореЗрдвреБрдВ рд╕реЗрдХреНрддреБрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫреЗрдпрдореН (рдШреГрддрдореН) рд╕рдВрджреАрдкреНрддрдВ рддреЗрдЬрдГ (рдЕрд╕реНрдп) рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗрдГ (рдпреЛрдирд┐рдГ) рдХрд╛рд░рдгрдореН (рдШреГрддреЗ) рдЖрдЬреНрдпреЗ (рд╢реНрд░рд┐рддрдГ) рд╕реЗрд╡рд┐рддрдГ (рдШреГрддрдореН) рддреЗрдЬрдГ (рдЙ) (рдЕрд╕реНрдп) (рдзрд╛рдо) рдЕрдзрд┐рдХрд░рдгрдореН (рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрд╡рдзрдореН) рд╕реНрд╡рдзрд╛рдордиреБрдЧрддрдВ рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрдореН (рдЖ) (рд╡рд╣) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╣рд┐ (рдорд╛рджрдпрд╕реНрд╡) рдЖрдирдиреНрджрдпрд╕реНрд╡ (рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд╣рд╛рдХреГрддрдореН) рд╕рддреНрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрдпрд╛ рдирд┐рд╖реНрдкрд╛рджрд┐рддрдореН (рд╡реГрд╖рдн) рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда (рд╡рдХреНрд╖рд┐) (рд╣рд╡реНрдпрдореН) рдЧреНрд░рд╣реАрддреБрдорд░реНрд╣рдореН реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рдпреЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗрд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рд░рд┐рд╡реЛрдкрдХрд╛рд░рдХрд╛рдГ рдкрд░реЛрдкрдХрд╛рд░рдорд╛рд╢реНрд░рд┐рддреНрдп рдЕрдиреНрдпрд╛рдиреН рд╕реБрдЦрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рдпрдордкрд┐ рддреИрд░реВрдкрдХреГрддрд╛ рдЖрдирдиреНрджрд┐рддрд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ реерезрезрееред рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╕реВрдХреНрддреЗрд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рдЪрд░рдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдореН рее рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдордгреНрдбрд▓реЗ рддреГрддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рддреНрд░рдпреЛрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рдЬреА рдорд╛рдгрд╕реЗ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддреАрд▓ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреАрдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгреЗ рдЙрдкрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░реВрди, рдкрд░реЛрдкрдХрд╛рд░рд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдЖрд╢реНрд░рдпрд╛рдиреЗ рдЗрддрд░рд╛рдВрдирд╛ рд╕реБрдЦреА рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд рддрд╕реЗ рд╕реНрд╡рддрдГрд╣реА рдЙрдкрдХреГрдд рд╣реЛрдКрди рдЖрдирдВрджрд┐рдд рд╣реЛрддрд╛рдд. рее резрез рее
